Me:"Hi, can I buy a Galaxy Mega?"

Yet, instead of treating my wounds, the staff decided to subject me to psychiatric interrogation which eventually led to forced confinement.

The staff's conduct toward mental health patients is ethically and legally questionable. A contract psychiatrist there (Said Jacob, an Egyptian with a record of probation) smelled an opportunity to make some easy money and invoked the California law 5150 (involuntary civil commitment) so he could detain me to the psych hospital (Aurora Charter Oak) where he also works as a contractor, though I didn't need it at all.

Worse yet, the staff in the ER seriously violated the due process outlined in the law. They didn't inform me why exactly I was going to be detained, what hospital I was being sent to, and what the nature of my detention was. Throughout the whole process I was purposefully kept in the dark. They alternately used deception ("You'll only stay there for a night") and intimidation ("We can call the police!") just trying to get me committed to the psych hospital. At one point, a female staff member even started yelling at me like a schoolyard bully.

It wasn't until I was thrown into Aurora Charter Oak that I realized I was put on a 72-hour hold, the reason being that I was "a danger to myself" (huh?). After the 72-hour hold expired, I was additionally declared "a danger to others" (huh???) and put on a 14-day extension. Although I managed to get out of that hellhole on the 10th day, this whole experience left me traumatized.

If you are a person with mental health problems, DO NOT, under any circumstances, go to the ER at San Dimas Community Hospital or something awful will happen to you.</Review>< Date>

Excellent workout. Straight up the fire service road for about 3 miles. Best to go early before the sun comes out strong since the road is fully exposed and has very little shade. Take plenty of water because it is not available once you get there. Keep in mind a 90 degree will sap your energy and hydration is a must. It takes about an hour to get up to Henninger Flats give or take a few minutes.</Text>

<user>102358566443682745574</user><gmapID>0x80c2dd2201383f4b:0x21496be732eb4eb3</gmapID><time>1574362591630</time><Text>It's a great place to hike to from Eaton Canyon... If you're NEW pay attention! There is a "contributor" Tatiana Lopez that appears to have uploaded 2500+ photos and tagged them as being taken at Henninger Flats. They are NOT properly tagged... and I've exhausted reported as many as I can... but it will take forever! So just ignore her photos... there is a very obvious difference in her photos verses what others have posted/tagged.

For those Hiking up from Eaton Canyon... it is a challenging elevation climb, but an easy hike as the trail is quite clear and wide. The trail is the "fire road" that leads up to Henninger (which was repaired a number of years ago after a landslide took out large portions of the road (and mountain side)... I'm glad it was reopened... and for those wanting a big challenge you can continue up to Mt. Wilson if you're feeling bold!

Remember to "leave no trace" and keep your 10 essentials with you. This is still wild country with spiders, snakes, bears and mountain lions in the area. So please, don't treat your hike as if you're going to Tom Sawyer Island and Disneyland. You can get hurt if you're not being safe. People have fallen from ledges and been hurt (a few killed) so treat nature with respect and stay firmly on the trails.

YIS,
-Bradley</Text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Rate>5<//Rate><Response>None<//Response></record>

<user_name>Joshua & Darby<//user_name>< Time>
1619713513137</Time>
<Text>In May I made the move from Seattle to Los Angeles and it didn‚Äôt take long for me to start itching to get outdoors and explore. Unfortunately it took me a couple weeks to settle in and finally make time to get out. I started doing some research on recommended places to camp near LA and Henniger Flats was at the top of almost everyone‚Äôs list that I could find online. A short hike, free camping and not far from where I live; sold. Especially for my first camping adventure since making the move to sunny California.

Henniger Flats is located in the San Gabriel Mountains near Altadena, California. Directions on getting there are pretty simple coming from downtown LA.

The trailhead to Henniger Flats is located off N Altadena Drive. It‚Äôs not easy to spot but if you‚Äôre familiar with the area, you‚Äôll probably have no problem finding it. If you‚Äôre heading to Henniger Flats for the night, you‚Äôll have to pay attention to where you park because there‚Äôs not a lot of overnight or long-term parking at the trailhead. I personally parked down the street on N Altadena in the neighborhood. Just keep an eye out for parking signs and you‚Äôll probably be ok.

When you reach the trailhead you‚Äôll see a sign that reads, ‚ÄúThe Henniger Flats Project.‚Äù You have to hike up  Mount Wilson Toll Road to get there. Initially it‚Äôs a little confusing to figure out which trail you need to be on to get there, at least it was for me. You‚Äôll walk down the beginning of the trail and cross the white bridge. Once you cross the white bridge, stay to the left and head up until you reach Henniger Flats. It‚Äôs about a 3 mile hike and the incline gets steep at times. There are plenty of benches to rest at on the way up.

There‚Äôs no shade on the way up so it‚Äôs important to start your hike early if you intend on camping and have a heavy pack. Also bring an abundance of water. There is a visitor center and museum at Henniger Flats, but there‚Äôs no running water. Be prepared! I didn‚Äôt run into any wildlife and you probably won‚Äôt either since the trail is very popular and there seems to be a lot of foot traffic throughout the day. There are a few signs for rattlesnakes but I didn‚Äôt run into any.

After your 3 mile journey to the top, you‚Äôve reached Henniger Flats. First thing‚Äôs first, you need to find the onsite LACFD Forester that‚Äôs on duty to check in. I read that you‚Äôll be given a permit for camping and to use a stove, but I didn‚Äôt have to do that when I checked in for whatever reason. There was a cub scout clan doing some work at the campgrounds so I‚Äôm sure he was busy and distracted. After or even before you check in, you can check out the visitor center and museum to learn about Henniger Flats and the surrounding areas. It‚Äôs pretty neat.

Once you get checked in you‚Äôll have to find your camping lot. There are 3 levels of camping at Henniger Flats. There‚Äôs a lower level campground near the visitor center and museum. It seemed pretty busy, so I walked to the upper and Fiji campgrounds. The forester actually recommended the Fiji campground area for a quieter environment and great place for setting up hammocks. He was absolutely right and if you‚Äôre looking for a quiet place to chillax, Fiji is the way to go.

Most larger camping lots have picnic tables and stoves to cook on. It‚Äôs worth noting there are about 15-20 camping lots in the upper and lower campgrounds. Fiji only has 3 camping lots, so you have to get there early to snag one. You can also call the forester head of time to get some insight on open camp lots. There‚Äôs plenty of shade once you get settled and the campgrounds are very well kept. There was no trash, the trails were well maintained and the views are phenomenal. There‚Äôs plenty of trails to check out after you get settled in.

Overall I had a great experience camping at Henniger Flats and I will certainly go again. #LosAngeles #Hiking #Outdoors< /Text></record></dataset><record>

<text>As I've said on other reviews.  I like pastrami.  Who doesn't?  I've had a love/hate relationship with Togo's from my first experience in the 1970's in Citrus Heights until the present.  It seems that the chain has difficulties between providing quality and providing less expensive sandwiches.    Every few years, prices go up, and quality with it.  Then it appears they choose not to raise prices again, and quality decreases for a few years until they raise prices again.  I've enjoyed Togo's pastrami sandwiches (#9 and #10) for many years in many locations, but at this time, it seems that they give you a lot of bread, and not much in the way of filling.  Honestly, I'd rather pay a bit more and get something with a bit more beef.  But on the other hand, what you do get it fairly good.  I say 3 stars.  Attached is a picture of one of their #10's front and back.  Lot of bread, not much filling.    But reasonably tasty.  From 12/6/2019.</text></record>

<rate>1< /rate>< review>
BEWARE  DO NOT USE THIS  PLACE.....
So my partner  accidentally booked this place. we only saw, the review's  after...  stories of bed bugs, cockroaches, Unsecure  rooms and people living on-site  as  permanent residents  were plentiful. we thought  we would still give it a chance. Upon arriving  the town seemed pretty desolate, isolated and forgotten. felt like being in a time warp. However It had a certain charm.

All seemed well that's until we noticed  no additional latch or secondary  lock on the door. The window in the bath room was unsecure and faced a liquor store that was open most of the night.we had to improvise  further security measures. But even after  all that   we still gave it a chance.

But late at night, as we tried to sleep we noticed...  bed bugs on the  mattress and inaddition  my partner  found cockroaches  in the  bathroom crawling all over our toothbrushes üò°.It  being midnight we decided to sleep  in our  car rental.  How are places like these still  allowed to do business  on booking...?? poor tourist  being subjected to  third world like treatment. I never had this issue in india. Shame  on you booking.<//review>
